text:
Wonderful!!!
I took the advise of other reviews and did 1cup white sugar and 1cup Brown sugar. I also used an electric mixer. The batter was so creamy, I ate alot of it raw(yummmm). I did have to cook it for an extra 15 minutes to get it done. I also toasted my pecans in a pan with butter flavored Pam before I put them in the batter. I sprayed both pans with Butter flavored Pam then sprinkled cinnamon and brown sugar(mixed) in the bottom of each pan added the batter then sprinkled the top of each with the cinnamon sugar mixture. Both came out of the pan clean and the top was sooooo good. I got this idea from another review as well. 
I looked at every recipe on this site before I decided on this one. I only found two reviews that were negative for this recipe and I have decided the cook must have done something wrong or their oven was not working properly. 
I am very pleased and will make this often!

I have a reputation at work as being our best baker, but I didn't have a banana bread recipe I was confident to share...until now!  I made this for the first time tonight with a few substitutions:  half shortening/half applesauce; removed 1 c. of the sugar; added 1 tsp. cinnamon and 1/2 tsp. nutmeg.  It turned out perfectly moist and delicious.  NOW I have to decide IF I'm even going to take one of the loaves to work!  Thanks, Teri Lynn for a classic recipe to add to my recipe box!

text:
This is for you chocolate lovers!  
I am a total nonconformist when it comes to baking.  I used 1C white sugar and 1C brown sugar.  I also took out about 1.5C of the batter and put it into a small bowl.  I added 1.5 Tb. of cocoa powder, 1Tb. of white sugar, 1Tb melted butter and chocolate chip.  Mix that all up, pour the banana batter into bread pans and drop the chocolate banana batter on top.  Take a butter knife and swirl it all around.  Super Yummy!

text:
I've made this recipe several times now and have made adjustments as I've gone.  I think it's perfect now.  I substituted 2 sticks (1 cup) of butter for the 1 cup of shortening. I substituted 1 cup of brown sugar for 1 cup of the white sugar.  I also added 1 tsp. cinnamon to the dry ingredients before combining them with the wet ingredients.  
In addition to this, I cut down on the baking time by baking them at 325 degrees, and making 12 jumbo muffins instead of the 2 loaves. 
 This recipe is the perfect amount for 12 jumbo muffins.
Very good flavor with the brown sugar and cinnamon, thanks for the recipe.

text:
Nice basic banana bread. I made this recipe as small gift loaves so I needed a bigger volume recipe. I used whole wheat white flour, cut the sugar back to one cup (my bananas were nice and ripe--no need for that much sugar) and because I am low on butter, I used a half cup of melted butter and substituted half homemade organic applesauce and half low-fat vanilla yogurt. I also added 3/4 teaspoon of nutmeg to lightly spice the loaves. I got 5 small gift loaves out of this one recipe, 1 1/2 cups batter to each loaf pan. 350 degrees for just over 30 minutes each and I was all set. Great recipe for me to use a surplus of ripe bananas and I was able to provide a random act of kindness for several people. NOTE: When I made this, I melted and cooled my butter, then wisked it into the wet ingredients. I wisked together the dry ingredients and folded the dry ingredients into the wet. This prevents overmixing and your bread dosen't peak up in the middle or turn out tough.

text:
Excellent! This b.bread hits the mark with super moistness and 'breadyness'. This is not the puddingy, gummy kind of b.bread...it's dense yet the 2 loaves baked up quite nicely (compared to any other b.bread I've made). The only tip I have is..make sure your bananas are super ripe, mine were just turning and I think it effected the depth of the banana flavor in my bread. The loaves were still wonderful and gone in a flash. This is now the only banana bread recipe I will use. Thanks Teri

text:
I made this bread and it is awful.  Crisp on the outside, a gooey, uncooked mess inside. While cooling, it fell flat in the middle.  Determined to find out what went wrong, I consulted an old Better Homes and Gardens cookbook which features a banana nut bread recipe I made years ago without a problem.  I was surprised to find that both recipes use all the same ingredients, with just vanilla added to this one, but it also has one glaring omission:  the bh&g recipe calls for baking POWDER, in addition to baking soda. I believe adding baking powder will prevent the collapse.  Also BH&G uses half the sugar (I know some reviewers said this recipe is too sweet).  And BH&G says to cook the bread at 350 degrees (not 300) for 45 to 50 minutes, which means the bread will bake throughout. I think the changes made in this recipe when compared to the old tried and true BH&G one ruined a wonderful bread.

text:
When a recipe has so many stellar reviews, I rarely bother with the low-star comments - but in this case, I wish I had, as the problems I had with this banana bread were exactly echoed by other members. I halved the recipe and followed it exactly, and my bread took 1 hour 40 minutes to bake at 300 degrees - as a result, it was too dark on the outside and the very middle was still slightly underdone.

After looking at 10+ other banana bread recipes, I notice that the vast majority called for being baked at 350 degrees. Most also added baking powder to the mix, which this recipe lacked. The flavor is good, though not quite as rich with banana flavor as I like, and the ingredients are convenient so I may try it again. But I would add 1/2 - 1 tsp of baking powder and bake at 350 degrees for 50 - 60 minutes. The recipe, as written, just doesn't work for single batches.

I made this twice in the past month. The second time I made it, I added a 1/2tsp nutmeg, a tsp cinammon, and  a 1/2 tsp allspice. I also browned some walnut bits and almond slices in  1 1/2 tbsp butter, about a tbsp brown sugar,and cinnamon sugar. Then I added 3/4 of that mixture to one of the loaves batter, and sprinkled the remaining on top of the loaf before baking it. And the last change I made was to dust the pan with cinnamon sugar. The additions were a nice and delicious change but the origianl recipe is just as good.I suggest only making the changes I made if you like a sweeter banana bread with more spices and a crunchy  nutty top.  I only added the nuts to one of the breads but both times I made this recipe I did dust the pans with cinammon sugar.

Made this recipe tonight and followed the ingredients exactly.  I added less than one cup of roasted pecans to the recipe and placed whole pecans on top then sprinkled it with a cinnamon/sugar mixture. I baked it in a 300 degree oven for 1 hour and 10 minutes, and although it looked perfect, it was too well done. The inside of the cake was browned halfway up to the top;  I also added the 2 1/2 cups white sugar (scant) and it was a little too sweet.  I will make this again, but will cook it less time and use two cups of sugar.  I did not find the cake as moist as the other reviewers, but probably because it baked too long.

text:
I've been searching for the perfect banana bread...very flavorful, moist, banana-ey....and this is the best out of all the recipes I've tried. It's perfect. The only substitution I make is using yogurt instead of shortening. It's healthier...changes the texture to make it a little less crumbly and more chewy like bread, but in a good way. For variations try using cream cheese or sour cream or applesauce in place of oil or in this case shortening and if you wanna play around with the flavors try adding fresh/frozen fruit (strawberry banana bread is a good combination) or using peanut butter. This is my permanent base recipe for banana bread now and good by itself or with any of my tinkering when Im in the mood for something different! Happy baking! Yummy!!
Ps: walnuts are sooo good in this. Makes about 24 muffins if any one is curious, although I guess it depends on your muffin size.

I adjusted size as I had 7 bananas. (Calculated for 34 servings.) This made 2 loaves and about 18 muffins.  I made this tonight using 1 1/2 cup egg substitute and per suggestions, used 2/3 cup applesauce & 2/3 cup oil for the shortening. I used 3 cups a.p. flour and 2 cups whole wheat, 1 cup white sugar, 2 cups packed brown sugar. Also added a 1 tsp cinnamon and 2 tsp cardamom, and 2 cups of chopped walnuts.  This was very good.  Moist and not too sweet.  Thanx, Teri Lynn, for this wonderful recipe.

I had lost my old favorite - this more than made up for it! I added chopped nuts, because we love 'em in our banana bread, but this was so good it would have still been 5 stars without them. Moist and delicious :-)
One suggestion, that I've used for years with sweet breads of all sorts: instead of flouring the greased pan I use sugar, or in this case cinnamon sugar - it makes a lovely additional crunch and flavor rather than that floury taste, and works just as well.

This is THE BEST!  I followed the advice of other reviewers by using 1 c. brown sugar and 1 c. granulated sugar; I also used substituted butter for half of the shortening with great results.  Sprinkling the loaf generously with the cinnamon-sugar mixture is a must!  This creates a moist crust with a unique look.  This loaf is dense and moist; if you're looking for light and cakey, search elsewhere.  By far the best banana bread recipe I've found to date.   I even received great compliments from someone who normally doesn't like banana bread!  Do yourself a favor and try this once--you'll never try another recipe.

Overall I would say this recipe is good, but it just isn't quite what I've been looking for.  I did take the advise from some other reviews and instead of 2 1/2 c. sugar, I used 1 c. sugar and 1 c. packed brown sugar.  I also added 1 tsp. of cinnamon and 1/2 tsp. nutmeg. This did turn out very good, but I was just looking for something heavier than this.  This recipe is very cake-like, which isn't bad and I would make this again, it just wasn't what I was looking for this time!

I followed the advice of several of the previous reviewers and changed a few things: 2 tsp. cinnamon, 1/2 tsp. nutmeg, 1/4 tsp cloves; used half white and half brown sugar; used pecans instead of walnuts (it's what I had)and I used 2 cups, chopped; sprinkled brown sugar/cinnamon blend on bottom of greased pan and on top of batter in the pan. The loaves come out quite easily and have a nice, sweet crunchy topping. I did have to cook the bread about 15 minutes longer but still very worth it. The best banana bread I have ever made. Everyone asks me to make this again and again. Thank you Teri Lynn for posting this recipe and thanks to the reviewers for adding the finishing touches!!!!!

I love to make Banana Bread and up UNTIL NOW my family really didn't care for it as much as I did.  This recipe, along with the suggestions of others made this the best Banana Bread I ever made.  Moist yet not oily.  I substituted some Wheat Flour for all the white flour.  I think it adds something to the bread.  I just always have done this.  About 1/3 of the flour was wheat. I made 3 loaves b/c I had lots of bananas and it was really fantastic.  You won't be disappointed!  They also freeze great!!

This bread is OK. I took the advice of other members and added lots of cinnamon and some nutmeg. I also used 1/2 brown sugar, and 1/2 white, and added 3/4 cup of chocolate chips. I read some of the reviews of others as well, and added about 1/2 tbsp of baking powder.  However, the bread still fell a little, and I did NOT open the oven until after about 50 minutes. It took a LOT longer to bake than the specified time, even though I made more, smaller loaves.The batter tasted really good, and I will try and make this again, but will add more baking powder, and cut out 1/2 cup of sugar, whether or not I add chocolate chips. It was rather sweet. I should add, too, that I had made this to give to my neighbor as a thank-you for helping me, but in light of the fact that it fell a little, I didn't think it looked good enough. But my husband and I enjoyed it, and froze some of it as well. I am not writing this one off, but it needs a few more tweaks.

Super easy.  I've made banana bread quite a few times and wanted to try a new recipe.  I added all my wet ingredients then in a separate bowl mixed all my dry ingredients then put them together.  Instead of shortening I used vegetable oil and I added 1 1 1/2 tsp of baking powder.  And I made banana bread muffins, before I put them in the oven I sprinkled cinnoman sugar on top.  They came out very good.  Made the top have a crunch. And baking powder made it fluffy.  I got the idea from another persons post for the top it was a great idea.  Easy enough for a beginner.  Next mission is to try it with Apple sauce to cut down on sugar since this recipe has just as much sugar as there is flour.  :)

text:
Have finally decided to rate this recipe after making it dozens of times over the past year or two. This is definitely the best banana bread recipe I have tried. The one thing I do differently is cut down on the sugar and use only about 3/4 of what is called for and use half white sugar and half brown. I usually make this in a mini(ish) loaf pan - that kind that has room for 4 small loaves.  I have found that 1 banana per loaf works perfectly. So if you happen to have one or two bananas on hand that are starting to get pretty brown that no one wants to eat anymore (like happens at my house) just adjust down and voila!

text:
Hands down, the best banana bread recipe I've ever seen!! I've done the recipe exactly as written and I've also changed a few things.  Either way, it's amazing!! It makes 2 loaves and comes out perfect everytime!  
I highly recommend it! 
Another variation is to use 1/2 c. butter and 1/2 c. shortening.  I always use the butter flavor crisco sticks.  I always use mexican vanilla (you cannot get a better vanilla taste)! I've also substituted 1c. brown sugar instead of using all white sugar.  It turns out about the same either way.  One trick is to grease the pan, then coat in brown sugar before you pour in your batter.  this way, it has a nice crust and everyone seems to really love that!

text:
I did not think this bread was the best that I have made. However, I prefer a much denser bread and this was more cake like. I cut the sugar down to 2 C and did 1/2 white and 1/2 brown sugar and it was still too sweet for our tastes. I took many suggestions on this site and used 1/2 butter and 1/2 veg oil. Added some cinnamon/sugar to bottom of pan and they just popped right out. They did rise very nicely and baked nice although a bit too brown for our liking as well. I don't like the bread to be really dark on sides and bottom and this was because it took that long to get done. I can't say that I would make this again only because I have other recipes that are more dense that I much prefer. It is very moist and cake like if that is what you prefer.

I loved this recipe, the bread was very moist and delicious. I did change a few things, I used 1 1/4c. white sugar and 1 1/4 cup brown sugar. I also used 2 more bananas for extra flavoring. I added the brown sugar sprinkled on the bottom of the pan, like another recommended, that was delicious. I also put a bit of butter mixed with brown sugar on top when the bread was just about done, it melted from the heat and formed a glaze. It was so good that my brother who is a chef himself, took over a half of loaf home, saying that everyone else had enough already!

text:
VEGAN VERSION

I used flax seed n'eggs instead of the eggs (Grind flax seeds in a coffee grinder...1/4 cup seeds pre-grinding per 3/4 cup cold water...1/3 of that mixture makes 1 n'egg...so make sure you use enough for the eggs called for).

I used non-hydrogenated vegan margerine.  Earth Balance.  YUM!

I used one extra banana for extra moistness.  

SO good.  SO dense.  SO moist.  Quite easy.

OH, and I used mostly brown sugar as well.

text:
This banana bread is awesome. I've made it at least 3 times and it's definitely in my "greatest hits" culinary catalog. I use brown sugar in place of white, though it's great both ways. I add 1 teaspoon of cinnamon & 1 cup of chopped pecans and it's heavenly. Baking time for me always seems to be a bit slow, and as a perfectionist I always like to keep a close watch on this bread and time-test it every so often to avoid under/overbaking. I also vary my pan sizes but usually get 1 big and one small pan loaf or 3 small pan loaves. Great to eat for breakfast or a pre-workout energy snack.

text:
I have used this recipe for years.  The shortening keeps this bread so lush and moist.  I agree with the brown sugar.  The first time I made this in early 2000 or 2001, I automatically did a combo of the sugars, dark brown and white.  I have found that brown sugar and dark brown add a little more body to baked food and sauces.  Refined white sugar tends to be flat.  I find I need more refined white sugar too.

text:
I'm rating this delicious recipe 5 stars even tho' I made many changes - I know, I know - but only because if it was so good w my changes that I can only imagine how good it would be as is. And for those who appreciate, as I do, the sharing of changes that might be of help to others, here were mine (changes only) for a 1/2 recipe that was lower sugar & carbs, higher protein:  3 very ripe bananas; A/P, buckwheat, & almond flours (30% each); Kerrigold unsalted butter; 3/4 cup Xylitol, 1/2 cup coconut sugar; & added 1/2 tsp BP, 2 tsp molasses, heaping 1/2 tsp cinnamon & 1 Tbsp each ground flax & chia seeds. Other ingredients were as written for half the recipe. Made 15 muffins (3/4 full), baked at 325 deg for 35 min (next time will try 30 min). 
   Just absolutely moist & delicious on 1st & 3rd day, but best on the 2nd day. A little sweet for me personally, so next time I'll reduce the coconut sugar by 2-4 Tbsp but increase molasses. 
     Please don't hesitate to try this recipe. If my picky 32 yr old daughter loved it, I can't imagine anyone who won't. Even my 9 yr old banana-hating granddaughter loved it!  :-D

This recipe is delicious, but I had a few problems with it.  I made a loaf and 14 muffins.  I made the mistake of putting the loaf in the oven then filling up the muffin pans and putting them in a few minutes later.  As a result, the bread fell.  But the muffins fell, too, so I don't know what I did wrong with them!  I baked the muffins for 40 minutes, but they were not done.  I ended up baking them for 55 minutes and they are still very moist.   I also baked the loaf an extra 15 minutes. They taste great, so next time I will try baking at 350 and I will NOT open the oven door!  Maybe then they will come out perfect.

This was a good bread for my first time making banana bread.  I found it a bit tough for our taste and only used 3 bananas, added some chocolate chips because my kids won't eat anything without chocolate, and put a brown sugar streusel on top. I also substituted half sweetened applesauce for half the shortening; maybe that's why I found it to be a bit tough.  I baked it for the recquired hour, too. Hmmmm, I will try this again to the letter because my family did enjoy it, and it smelled heavenly while baking!
ETA:  Ok, made it again today (3-17-06) This time added more banana and chunks of chocolate, but used only shortening and no applesauce.  Baked it for one hour and it tasted DELICIOUS (with its streusal topping), but this time it fell in the middle! Next time, I'll do it the same, but bake it for a longer time.
